Following the Religion of Old Women: Consensus, Not Blind Imitation
Clarifying the intent behind the Salaf's saying.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Salaf's saying 'hold fast to the religion of old women' is a command to adhere to their consensus, not an endorsement of blind imitation (taqlid).

Core Idea
The 'religion of old women' means following the Salaf's consensus, not blind imitation.

The author addresses a common misunderstanding: some people cite the saying 'hold fast to the religion of old women' to justify blind imitation (taqlid) in matters of creed. However, the author clarifies that the intended meaning is to adhere to the agreed-upon teachings of the righteous Salaf, which even the uneducated can follow, and to abandon the innovations of later sects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Pay attention to the author's main claim about the saying.
2
Identify the author's refutation
The author says the saying does not prove taqlid. Understand why: because the command is to follow the consensus of the Salaf, not to blindly imitate without evidence.
The Salaf's consensus is based on knowledge transmitted from the Prophet.
3
Notice the phrase 'those not qualified for nazar'
The author mentions that the consensus has reached even old women, children, and Bedouins. This shows the teachings are accessible, not that taqlid is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الثاني - وهو ما حكاه عن بعض السلف مِنْ قوله : ( عليكم ـ بدين العجائز ) - : فلا دليلَ فيهِ أيضاً على صحة التقليد ؛ لأنَّ مراد هذا القائل : الأمرُ بالتمسُّكِ بما اجتمعَ عليه السلف الصالحُ مِنَ الصحابة والتابعين حتى وصل علمُهُ إلى مَنْ ليسَ أهلاً للنظرِ ؛ كالعجائز ، والصبيان في الكتاب ، والأعراب أهل البدو ، وترك ما أحدثه المبتدعةُ مِنَ القدريَّةِ والمرجئة والجبرية والروافض وغيرِهم ممَّا لا وجود له في أعصارِ السلف الصالح خاصهم وعامهم ، وذكرُ أمثلة ذلك على الاستيفاء يطولُ ، ولنذكرِ البعض ليتبيَّنَ بهِ المراد : فمِنْ ذلكَ : ما أحدثه المعتزلة مِنْ تقييد إرادة الله جل وعلا بالطاعة ، وأنَّ الكفر والمعاصي لم يُرِدْها اللهُ عزَّ وجلَّ ، وإِنَّما العباد أوقعوا ما لم يُرِدْهُ اللهُ جلَّ وعزَّ ، ومعلوم أنَّ هذهِ ضلالةٌ لا مستند لها ، وإِنَّما الذي اشتهر في زمن السلف الصالح وتلقاه منهم الخلف ، ولَهِجَ بهِ الصغير والكبير ، والذكر والأنثى ، والحـرُّ والعبد ، والحاضر والبادي ، حتى صار كَأَنَّهُ معلومٌ مِنْ دينِ المسلمينَ ضرورةً ، يَلهَجُ بهِ مَنْ عرف معناهُ ومَنْ لم يعرف .. وقوع الكائنات كلها بإرادةِ اللهِ تعالى ، وأنَّ ما شاءَ اللهُ كانَ ، وما لم يشأ لم يكن ، إنَّ جهلة العصاة يعتذرونَ عن معاصيهم بإرادة الله تعالى منهم حتى
As for the second (issue) – which he narrated from some of the Salaf, namely his saying: 'Hold fast to the religion of old women' – there is no proof in it for the validity of blind imitation (taqlid). Because the intended meaning of this speaker is: the command to adhere to what the righteous Salaf – the Companions and the Followers – agreed upon, until its knowledge reached those who are not qualified for independent investigation (nazar), such as old women, children in the writing school, and Bedouin Arabs, and to abandon what the innovators – such as the Qadariyya, Murji'a, Jabriyya, Rawafid, and others – have invented, which have no existence in the eras of the righteous Salaf, both their elite and their commoners. And enumerating examples of that at length would be lengthy, so we will mention a part to clarify the intent: Among that is what the Mu'tazila innovated by restricting the will of Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, to obedience, and that disbelief and acts of disobedience were not willed by Allah, the Exalted and Majestic, and that the servants only brought about what Allah did not will. It is known that this is a misguidance with no basis. What was widespread in the time of the righteous Salaf, and the successors received it from them, and both young and old, male and female, free and slave, resident and Bedouin became accustomed to – until it became as if it were necessarily known from the religion of the Muslims – that all things that occur happen by the will of Allah, the Exalted, and that what Allah wills comes to be and what He does not will does not come to be. Indeed, the ignorant sinners excuse their sins by [saying that] they occur by the will of Allah, the Exalted, from them until
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim that the saying 'Hold fast to the religion of old women' supports blind imitation (taqlid). The author first explains that the intended meaning of this saying is the command to adhere to the consensus of the righteous Salaf (the Companions and Followers) and to avoid the innovations of the sects (Qadariyya, Murji'a, Jabriyya, Rawafid). The knowledge of this consensus has reached even those who are not qualified for independent reasoning (nazar), such as old women, children, and Bedouins. He then gives a specific example of innovation: the Mu'tazila's restriction of Allah's will to obedience only, denying that He wills disbelief and sins. Instead, they claim that servants bring about what Allah did not will. The author declares this a clear misguidance. He then contrasts it with the universal belief of the Salaf and the laity: that all things occur by Allah's will, that what He wills happens and what He does not will does not happen. This belief is so widespread that it is known as a necessary part of the religion. The author notes that ignorant sinners use this belief as an excuse for their sins (by claiming God willed their sins), but the key point is to affirm Allah's universal will while rejecting the Mu'tazila innovation.

Key Terms
تقليد
سلف
عجائز
نظر
مبتدعة
قدريّة
مرجئة
جبرية
روافض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The saying 'hold fast to the religion of old women' proves that blind imitation (taqlid) is acceptable.
Correction: The author explains that the command is to follow the consensus of the Salaf, which is based on transmitted knowledge, not to engage in blind imitation without evidence.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does the saying 'hold fast to the religion of old women' command?
A) Blind imitation of one's ancestors
B) Adhering to the consensus of the righteous Salaf and avoiding innovations
C) Following only the opinions of old women
D) Rejecting all independent reasoning

Key Takeaway
The Salaf's saying commands adherence to their consensus, not blind imitation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a belief simply because you were raised with it, without verifying if it aligns with the consensus of the Salaf? What was it, and what step could you take today to correct that?
?
The passage mentions that even an old woman can know the creed transmitted from the Salaf. Do you feel confident that the creed you hold is exactly what the Companions and Followers agreed upon, or have you unknowingly accepted ideas from later sects? How can you find out?
?
When you hear the phrase 'religion of old women,' does your heart move towards humility in following the transmitted truth, or do you feel a sense of superiority? What does your reaction reveal about your attitude towards the Salaf and their consensus?

Refuting the Mu'tazila: All Things Occur by Allah's Will
Refuting Mu'tazila on divine will and affirming Sunni doctrine.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila innovation of restricting God's will to obedience only and the orthodox Sunni affirmation that all things occur by Allah's will.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila wrongly restrict God's will; the truth is that all things happen by Allah's will.

The author provides an example of the innovation that the Salaf warned against: the Mu'tazila claim that Allah only wills obedience, not disbelief or sin. They argue that servants bring about what Allah did not will. The author declares this a clear misguidance and contrasts it with the universal belief of the Salaf that everything occurs by Allah's will.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and translation. Focus on the Mu'tazila position and the author's refutation.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila innovation
The Mu'tazila limit God's will to obedience only, claiming that sins occur without His will. Understand why this is problematic.
They deny God's universal will.
3
Learn the Sunni belief
The author states the belief that all things occur by Allah's will, known necessarily from the religion. Note how this was widespread among the Salaf.
This belief is affirmed even by the ignorant sinners who use it as an excuse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الثاني - وهو ما حكاه عن بعض السلف مِنْ قوله : ( عليكم ـ بدين العجائز ) - : فلا دليلَ فيهِ أيضاً على صحة التقليد ؛ لأنَّ مراد هذا القائل : الأمرُ بالتمسُّكِ بما اجتمعَ عليه السلف الصالحُ مِنَ الصحابة والتابعين حتى وصل علمُهُ إلى مَنْ ليسَ أهلاً للنظرِ ؛ كالعجائز ، والصبيان في الكتاب ، والأعراب أهل البدو ، وترك ما أحدثه المبتدعةُ مِنَ القدريَّةِ والمرجئة والجبرية والروافض وغيرِهم ممَّا لا وجود له في أعصارِ السلف الصالح خاصهم وعامهم ، وذكرُ أمثلة ذلك على الاستيفاء يطولُ ، ولنذكرِ البعض ليتبيَّنَ بهِ المراد : فمِنْ ذلكَ : ما أحدثه المعتزلة مِنْ تقييد إرادة الله جل وعلا بالطاعة ، وأنَّ الكفر والمعاصي لم يُرِدْها اللهُ عزَّ وجلَّ ، وإِنَّما العباد أوقعوا ما لم يُرِدْهُ اللهُ جلَّ وعزَّ ، ومعلوم أنَّ هذهِ ضلالةٌ لا مستند لها ، وإِنَّما الذي اشتهر في زمن السلف الصالح وتلقاه منهم الخلف ، ولَهِجَ بهِ الصغير والكبير ، والذكر والأنثى ، والحـرُّ والعبد ، والحاضر والبادي ، حتى صار كَأَنَّهُ معلومٌ مِنْ دينِ المسلمينَ ضرورةً ، يَلهَجُ بهِ مَنْ عرف معناهُ ومَنْ لم يعرف .. وقوع الكائنات كلها بإرادةِ اللهِ تعالى ، وأنَّ ما شاءَ اللهُ كانَ ، وما لم يشأ لم يكن ، إنَّ جهلة العصاة يعتذرونَ عن معاصيهم بإرادة الله تعالى منهم حتى
As for the second (issue) – which he narrated from some of the Salaf, namely his saying: 'Hold fast to the religion of old women' – there is no proof in it for the validity of blind imitation (taqlid). Because the intended meaning of this speaker is: the command to adhere to what the righteous Salaf – the Companions and the Followers – agreed upon, until its knowledge reached those who are not qualified for independent investigation (nazar), such as old women, children in the writing school, and Bedouin Arabs, and to abandon what the innovators – such as the Qadariyya, Murji'a, Jabriyya, Rawafid, and others – have invented, which have no existence in the eras of the righteous Salaf, both their elite and their commoners. And enumerating examples of that at length would be lengthy, so we will mention a part to clarify the intent: Among that is what the Mu'tazila innovated by restricting the will of Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, to obedience, and that disbelief and acts of disobedience were not willed by Allah, the Exalted and Majestic, and that the servants only brought about what Allah did not will. It is known that this is a misguidance with no basis. What was widespread in the time of the righteous Salaf, and the successors received it from them, and both young and old, male and female, free and slave, resident and Bedouin became accustomed to – until it became as if it were necessarily known from the religion of the Muslims – that all things that occur happen by the will of Allah, the Exalted, and that what Allah wills comes to be and what He does not will does not come to be. Indeed, the ignorant sinners excuse their sins by [saying that] they occur by the will of Allah, the Exalted, from them until

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim that the saying 'Hold fast to the religion of old women' supports blind imitation (taqlid). The author first explains that the intended meaning of this saying is the command to adhere to the consensus of the righteous Salaf (the Companions and Followers) and to avoid the innovations of the sects (Qadariyya, Murji'a, Jabriyya, Rawafid). The knowledge of this consensus has reached even those who are not qualified for independent reasoning (nazar), such as old women, children, and Bedouins. He then gives a specific example of innovation: the Mu'tazila's restriction of Allah's will to obedience only, denying that He wills disbelief and sins. Instead, they claim that servants bring about what Allah did not will. The author declares this a clear misguidance. He then contrasts it with the universal belief of the Salaf and the laity: that all things occur by Allah's will, that what He wills happens and what He does not will does not happen. This belief is so widespread that it is known as a necessary part of the religion. The author notes that ignorant sinners use this belief as an excuse for their sins (by claiming God willed their sins), but the key point is to affirm Allah's universal will while rejecting the Mu'tazila innovation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah only wills obedience, not sins; sins occur without His will.
Correction: The author declares this a misguidance; the correct belief is that all things occur by Allah's will, including sins, though He does not love them.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the belief that was widespread among the Salaf regarding God's will?
A) God only wills obedience
B) God wills only good deeds
C) All things occur by God's will
D) God does not involve Himself in human actions

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila innovation on God's will is refuted; the truth is that all things occur by Allah's will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every event in your life—including your own sins and shortcomings—occurs by Allah's will? How does that belief affect the way you repent and strive to change?
?
When you sin, do you ever find yourself excusing it by thinking 'Allah willed it'? Is that a sign of genuine reliance on qadr, or a cover for laziness? What would it take for you to take full responsibility for your actions while still believing in Allah's will?
?
This passage says the belief that all things occur by Allah's will is 'known necessarily from the religion of the Muslims.' Does your heart truly rest in that certainty, or do you sometimes doubt? What would it take for you to live with that conviction every moment?

The Scholars as Guardians of the Faith
Sanusi describes the scholars' role in preserving religion using inherited knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Sunni scholars, as inheritors of the Prophet's knowledge, used the treasures of revelation and reason to refute heretical doubts and preserve the religion for all Muslims.

Core Idea
Sunni scholars are the guardians who defend Islam using the treasures of revelation and reason.

In this opening segment of his defense, Imam al-Sanusi paints a vivid picture of the Sunni theologians as the protective fortress of Islam. He explains how they inherited profound knowledge from the Prophet and the early generations, which they deployed to dismantle the illusions of innovators. This lesson establishes their foundational role as the custodians of orthodox belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage attentively
Read the selected Arabic text once without pausing, then read the English translation. Notice the author's passionate tone.
2
Identify the scholars' resources
Sanusi mentions the 'treasures' (الذخائر) from the Book, Sunnah, and Companions. Why are these considered the most powerful tools against doubt?
3
Reflect on the fortress analogy
The Prophet left his community like a lion in a thicket with his cubs. What does this imagery convey about the protection provided to the early Muslims?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العلماءُ رضي الله عنهم في الاحتياط للدين ، ونظرَتْ بعين الرحمة لجميع المسلمينَ ، فأفسدَتْ عليهم تلك الشبهات ، وفسخَتْ لهم تلك الأوهام والتخيُّلاتِ ؛ بأجوبة قاطعة لا يجد العاقل عن الإذعانِ إليها سبيلاً ، وأنفقوا رضيَ الله عنهم في جميعِ ذلك الذخائر التي حصلت لهم مِنَ الكتاب والسنَّةِ وأصحاب رسولِ اللهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، الذينَ هُمُ القدوة لهذه الأمَّةِ ، وقد كان حرزُ الدين محفوظاً في عهدِ النبيَّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أنْ يتجاسر أحدٌ يرومُ الاختلاس منه ، وإنَّما تجاسرَ مَنْ تجاسر عندَ غَيبتِهِ ، لكن لم يمت صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ حتى وَرَّثَ علماءَ أُمَّتِهِ وأهلَ سُنَّتِهِ مِنَ المعارفِ ما يدفعونَ بِهِ كلَّ عدو يريدُ الاختلاس مِنْ دينهم أَحَلَّ أُمَّتَهُ فِي حِرْزِ مِلَّتِهِ كَاللَّيْثِ حَلَّ مَعَ الْأَشْبَالِ فِي أَجَمٍ فحين قدم الأعداء بعد موتِ النبيِّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ لهدم حصن الدين .. أنفقوا في تحصينه أعظم تحصين تلك الذخائر التي ورثوها واستعملوا آلاتِ عقولهم في وجوه إنفاقها ، ولم تزل أرباح تلكَ الذخائرِ مِنْ زيادةِ المعارفِ تتوالى عليهم ، وينفقونها عند الاحتياج إليها ، فهذا حال علماء السنَّةِ الذين تكلموا في علم التوحيدِ ، وألفوا فيه التواليف ، جزاهُمُ اللهُ أفضل جزاء . فبالله أيُّها المقلّد الذي يستدل بما لا يحيطُ بِهِ علماً ؛ مَنْ كانَ يقفُ لرد أهل البدع حين خاضوا معَ كثرتهم وعظيم احتيالهم في شبهاتِهم ، ولهم المنزلة في الدنيا بحيث يتمكنونَ بها مِنْ سَوْقِ الناسِ إلى أغراضهم .. لولا ما نهضَ لهم رجالُ اللهِ مِنَ العلماء الراسخين ؟! وأي دين يبقى لعجوز أو صبي أو مُقلّد لولا بركةُ أولئكَ العلماءِ رضيَ اللهُ عنهم ؟! وأي جهادٍ يوازي جهادَ هؤلاء العلماء ؟! وأي رباط يماثلُ رباطهم وعكوفَهم على استعمال العقولِ وتحبيسِها مُدَّةَ الحياة على الجَوَلانِ فيما يحفظ دين المسلمين ؟! فمهما لاحَ لهم مُختلِسٌ يريدُ شيئاً مِنَ الدينِ .. قابلوه بشهابٍ مِنْ نَيْراتِ البراهين ، فردُّوه خاسئاً لم ينقلب إلا بأعظم فضيحة ، وأينَ هذا الجهاد ورباطُهُ مِنْ جهادِ السيوف ورباط الثغور الذي غايتُهُ حفظ نفسٍ أو مالٍ لا بدَّ في الدنيا مِنْ فراقهما ، والأَوَّلُ حفظُ دين لو ذهب لهلك الناسُ في عذابِ جهنَّمَ أَبدَ الآبدين ؟! وقد رُوِيَ : أنَّ الأستاذ أبا إسحاق الإسفرايني رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ صَعِدَ في زمن هيجان المبتدعة إلى جبل لبنانَ ؛ وهو مُتعبدٌ لأولياء الله تعالى وخلوة لهم عن الناسِ ، فوجدَهم هنالك يتعبَّدونَ ، فقال لهم : يا أَكَلَةَ الحشيش ؛ هربتُم إلى هذا الموضع تتعبَّدون وتركتُم صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في أيدي المبتدعة ؟! فقالوا له : أَيُّها الأستاذ ؛ لا قدرة لنا على مخالطة الخلق ، وأنت الذي أقدرَكَ اللهُ على ذلكَ فأنت أهله ، فرجع رضي الله عنه واشتغل بالرد على المبتدعة ، وأَلَّفَ كتابه ( الجامع بينَ الجلي والخفيّ )
The scholars, may God be pleased with them, were cautious for the religion, and looked with the eye of mercy upon all Muslims, so they nullified those doubts for them, and refuted for them those illusions and fantasies, with decisive answers, to which a rational person finds no way but to submit. And they spent, may God be pleased with them, in all of that the treasures that they had obtained from the Book, the Sunnah, and the Companions of the Messenger of God, peace and blessings be upon him, who are the exemplars for this community. The fortress of religion was protected during the lifetime of the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, from anyone daring to try to steal from it; rather, those who dared only dared after his absence. But he did not die, peace and blessings be upon him, until he bequeathed to the scholars of his community and the people of his Sunnah from the sciences that which they would repel with every enemy who wanted to steal from their religion. He placed his community in the fortress of his religion like a lion in a thicket with his cubs. So when the enemies came after the death of the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, to demolish the fortress of religion, they spent in fortifying it the greatest fortification of those treasures they had inherited, and they used the tools of their intellects in the ways of spending them. And the profits of those treasures from the increase of sciences continued to come to them, and they spent them when needed. This is the state of the scholars of the Sunnah who spoke about the science of Tawhid and authored works on it, may God reward them with the best reward. By God, O blind follower who argues from what he does not fully know, who would have stood to refute the people of innovation when they plunged with their great number and immense cunning into their doubts, while they had status in this world such that they could drive people to their purposes, had not the men of God from the deeply rooted scholars risen against them? And what religion would remain for an old woman, a child, or a blind follower had it not been for the blessing of those scholars, may God be pleased with them? And what jihad equals the jihad of these scholars? And what border guard duty is like their border guard duty and their devotion to using intellects and dedicating them for life to roam in what preserves the religion of Muslims? So whenever a thief appeared to them wanting something from the religion, they confronted him with a meteor from the luminous proofs, and they repelled him, humiliated, and he returned only with the greatest disgrace. And where is this jihad and its border guard duty compared to the jihad of swords and the guard duty of frontiers, whose purpose is the preservation of life or wealth which inevitably must be parted from in this world? Whereas the former is preserving a religion which, if lost, people would perish in the punishment of Hell forever and ever. And it has been narrated that the master Abu Ishaq al-Isfara'ini, may God be pleased with him, ascended during a time of heretical agitation to Mount Lebanon, which was a place of worship for the saints of God and a retreat for them away from people. He found them there worshipping, and said to them: 'O eaters of hashish, you have fled to this place to worship and left the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, in the hands of the innovators?' They said to him: 'O master, we have no ability to mix with people, and you are the one whom God has enabled for that, so you are the one for it.' So he returned, may God be pleased with him, and occupied himself with refuting the innovators, and authored his book 'al-Jami' bayna al-Jali wa al-Khafi' (The Compendium of the Explicit and the Hidden).
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the Sunni scholars who engaged in kalam (theology) and wrote works on Tawhid. The author begins by praising these scholars for their cautiousness on behalf of the religion and their mercy towards all Muslims. He states that they refuted the doubts and illusions of heretics with decisive answers that no rational person could reject. They spent their treasures—knowledge inherited from the Quran, Sunnah, and Companions—to fortify the religion after the Prophet's death. The author then emphasizes that the Prophet himself wasqueathed these sciences to his scholars so they could repel enemies. After the Prophet's death, scholars used these treasures and their intellects to strengthen the religion, continually gaining more knowledge. The author then addresses a blind follower (muqallid) who cannot properly evaluate evidence, asking rhetorically who but the deeply rooted scholars could have refuted the innovators? He argues that without these scholars, no religion would remain for the weak and unlearned. He then compares the jihad of the scholars—intellectual struggle using proofs—to physical jihad with swords, declaring the former superior because it preserves the religion itself, eternal life saved from Hell, while physical jihad only preserves temporary life and wealth. Finally, he narrates an anecdote about Abu Ishaq al-Isfara'ini: during a time of heretical agitation, he found pious ascetics hiding in Mount Lebanon, and he rebuked them for neglecting the defense of the Prophet's community; they admitted their weakness and recognized his capability, so he returned to engage in refuting innovators and wrote a book.

Key Terms
شبهات
براهين
ذخائر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sunni theologians rely solely on reason and ignore revelation.
Correction: Sanusi emphasizes that they used treasures from the Book, Sunnah, and Companions, showing they are rooted in revelation.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what did the Prophet bequeath to the scholars?
A) Wealth and property
B) Political power
C) Sciences to defend the religion
D) Swords and weapons

Key Takeaway
Sunni scholars are the legitimate inheritors of the Prophet's knowledge, tasked with defending the religion using both revelation and reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to follow the Sunnah, but do you actually rely on the scholars' inherited treasures when doubts attack your faith, or do you depend on your own whims? What treasure have you personally received from the scholars that you actively use to guard your religion?
?
The Prophet bequeathed knowledge to the scholars so that they could defend the faith after his departure. Have you ever considered yourself as someone who inherits that knowledge? What responsibility does that place on you to defend your religion when you hear it being attacked?
?
The scholars used their intellects to fortify the religion, not just preserve it. When was the last time you used your intellect to deeply understand a matter of aqeedah instead of just repeating what you've heard? Are you content to be a passive follower or an active guardian?

The Superiority of Intellectual Jihad
Sanusi argues for the superiority of intellectual jihad and recounts a relevant anecdote.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi considers the intellectual struggle of scholars to be superior to physical military jihad, and how the anecdote of Abu Ishaq al-Isfara'ini illustrates this priority.

Core Idea
Defending the religion with proof is greater than defending it with the sword.

In the second part of this defense, Sanusi shifts to a powerful argument that the struggle of the theologian is the highest form of jihad. He challenges the blind follower to consider what would remain of Islam without the scholars' efforts, and then contrasts the intellectual defense of the faith with physical military defense. Finally, he relates a compelling story of Abu Ishaq al-Isfara'ini, who left his mountain retreat to confront innovators.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the rhetorical questions
Sanusi uses a series of questions to make his point. Notice how each question builds on the previous one.
2
Compare the two forms of jihad
He distinguishes between jihad of the sword (preserving life/wealth) and jihad of proof (preserving the religion). Which does he argue is more important and why?
3
Analyze the anecdote
What does Abu Ishaq's rebuke of the ascetics teach us about the duty of scholars? How does this story reinforce the main argument?

العلماءُ رضي الله عنهم في الاحتياط للدين ، ونظرَتْ بعين الرحمة لجميع المسلمينَ ، فأفسدَتْ عليهم تلك الشبهات ، وفسخَتْ لهم تلك الأوهام والتخيُّلاتِ ؛ بأجوبة قاطعة لا يجد العاقل عن الإذعانِ إليها سبيلاً ، وأنفقوا رضيَ الله عنهم في جميعِ ذلك الذخائر التي حصلت لهم مِنَ الكتاب والسنَّةِ وأصحاب رسولِ اللهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، الذينَ هُمُ القدوة لهذه الأمَّةِ ، وقد كان حرزُ الدين محفوظاً في عهدِ النبيَّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أنْ يتجاسر أحدٌ يرومُ الاختلاس منه ، وإنَّما تجاسرَ مَنْ تجاسر عندَ غَيبتِهِ ، لكن لم يمت صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ حتى وَرَّثَ علماءَ أُمَّتِهِ وأهلَ سُنَّتِهِ مِنَ المعارفِ ما يدفعونَ بِهِ كلَّ عدو يريدُ الاختلاس مِنْ دينهم أَحَلَّ أُمَّتَهُ فِي حِرْزِ مِلَّتِهِ كَاللَّيْثِ حَلَّ مَعَ الْأَشْبَالِ فِي أَجَمٍ فحين قدم الأعداء بعد موتِ النبيِّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ لهدم حصن الدين .. أنفقوا في تحصينه أعظم تحصين تلك الذخائر التي ورثوها واستعملوا آلاتِ عقولهم في وجوه إنفاقها ، ولم تزل أرباح تلكَ الذخائرِ مِنْ زيادةِ المعارفِ تتوالى عليهم ، وينفقونها عند الاحتياج إليها ، فهذا حال علماء السنَّةِ الذين تكلموا في علم التوحيدِ ، وألفوا فيه التواليف ، جزاهُمُ اللهُ أفضل جزاء . فبالله أيُّها المقلّد الذي يستدل بما لا يحيطُ بِهِ علماً ؛ مَنْ كانَ يقفُ لرد أهل البدع حين خاضوا معَ كثرتهم وعظيم احتيالهم في شبهاتِهم ، ولهم المنزلة في الدنيا بحيث يتمكنونَ بها مِنْ سَوْقِ الناسِ إلى أغراضهم .. لولا ما نهضَ لهم رجالُ اللهِ مِنَ العلماء الراسخين ؟! وأي دين يبقى لعجوز أو صبي أو مُقلّد لولا بركةُ أولئكَ العلماءِ رضيَ اللهُ عنهم ؟! وأي جهادٍ يوازي جهادَ هؤلاء العلماء ؟! وأي رباط يماثلُ رباطهم وعكوفَهم على استعمال العقولِ وتحبيسِها مُدَّةَ الحياة على الجَوَلانِ فيما يحفظ دين المسلمين ؟! فمهما لاحَ لهم مُختلِسٌ يريدُ شيئاً مِنَ الدينِ .. قابلوه بشهابٍ مِنْ نَيْراتِ البراهين ، فردُّوه خاسئاً لم ينقلب إلا بأعظم فضيحة ، وأينَ هذا الجهاد ورباطُهُ مِنْ جهادِ السيوف ورباط الثغور الذي غايتُهُ حفظ نفسٍ أو مالٍ لا بدَّ في الدنيا مِنْ فراقهما ، والأَوَّلُ حفظُ دين لو ذهب لهلك الناسُ في عذابِ جهنَّمَ أَبدَ الآبدين ؟! وقد رُوِيَ : أنَّ الأستاذ أبا إسحاق الإسفرايني رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ صَعِدَ في زمن هيجان المبتدعة إلى جبل لبنانَ ؛ وهو مُتعبدٌ لأولياء الله تعالى وخلوة لهم عن الناسِ ، فوجدَهم هنالك يتعبَّدونَ ، فقال لهم : يا أَكَلَةَ الحشيش ؛ هربتُم إلى هذا الموضع تتعبَّدون وتركتُم صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في أيدي المبتدعة ؟! فقالوا له : أَيُّها الأستاذ ؛ لا قدرة لنا على مخالطة الخلق ، وأنت الذي أقدرَكَ اللهُ على ذلكَ فأنت أهله ، فرجع رضي الله عنه واشتغل بالرد على المبتدعة ، وأَلَّفَ كتابه ( الجامع بينَ الجلي والخفيّ )
The scholars, may God be pleased with them, were cautious for the religion, and looked with the eye of mercy upon all Muslims, so they nullified those doubts for them, and refuted for them those illusions and fantasies, with decisive answers, to which a rational person finds no way but to submit. And they spent, may God be pleased with them, in all of that the treasures that they had obtained from the Book, the Sunnah, and the Companions of the Messenger of God, peace and blessings be upon him, who are the exemplars for this community. The fortress of religion was protected during the lifetime of the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, from anyone daring to try to steal from it; rather, those who dared only dared after his absence. But he did not die, peace and blessings be upon him, until he bequeathed to the scholars of his community and the people of his Sunnah from the sciences that which they would repel with every enemy who wanted to steal from their religion. He placed his community in the fortress of his religion like a lion in a thicket with his cubs. So when the enemies came after the death of the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, to demolish the fortress of religion, they spent in fortifying it the greatest fortification of those treasures they had inherited, and they used the tools of their intellects in the ways of spending them. And the profits of those treasures from the increase of sciences continued to come to them, and they spent them when needed. This is the state of the scholars of the Sunnah who spoke about the science of Tawhid and authored works on it, may God reward them with the best reward. By God, O blind follower who argues from what he does not fully know, who would have stood to refute the people of innovation when they plunged with their great number and immense cunning into their doubts, while they had status in this world such that they could drive people to their purposes, had not the men of God from the deeply rooted scholars risen against them? And what religion would remain for an old woman, a child, or a blind follower had it not been for the blessing of those scholars, may God be pleased with them? And what jihad equals the jihad of these scholars? And what border guard duty is like their border guard duty and their devotion to using intellects and dedicating them for life to roam in what preserves the religion of Muslims? So whenever a thief appeared to them wanting something from the religion, they confronted him with a meteor from the luminous proofs, and they repelled him, humiliated, and he returned only with the greatest disgrace. And where is this jihad and its border guard duty compared to the jihad of swords and the guard duty of frontiers, whose purpose is the preservation of life or wealth which inevitably must be parted from in this world? Whereas the former is preserving a religion which, if lost, people would perish in the punishment of Hell forever and ever. And it has been narrated that the master Abu Ishaq al-Isfara'ini, may God be pleased with him, ascended during a time of heretical agitation to Mount Lebanon, which was a place of worship for the saints of God and a retreat for them away from people. He found them there worshipping, and said to them: 'O eaters of hashish, you have fled to this place to worship and left the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, in the hands of the innovators?' They said to him: 'O master, we have no ability to mix with people, and you are the one whom God has enabled for that, so you are the one for it.' So he returned, may God be pleased with him, and occupied himself with refuting the innovators, and authored his book 'al-Jami' bayna al-Jali wa al-Khafi' (The Compendium of the Explicit and the Hidden).

This passage is a defense of the Sunni scholars who engaged in kalam (theology) and wrote works on Tawhid. The author begins by praising these scholars for their cautiousness on behalf of the religion and their mercy towards all Muslims. He states that they refuted the doubts and illusions of heretics with decisive answers that no rational person could reject. Understanding the Phrase 'Religion of Old Women'
Answering an objection about the phrase 'religion of old women'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the context and purpose behind the early scholars' use of the phrase 'religion of old women' and why it does not reject theological reasoning.

Core Idea
The 'religion of old women' was a safe refuge, not a rejection of theology.

You may have heard the phrase 'religion of old women' attributed to early scholars, sometimes used to dismiss theological inquiry. But what did they really mean? In this passage, we see that this statement was a protective measure during a time of rampant innovation, meant to guide the weak back to the pure faith taught by the Companions. Let's read the author's explanation and understand its true intent.

Guided Path
1
Consider the objection
The passage begins with an objection: if the intended meaning is to follow the Companions, why use vague wording like 'religion of old women'? Notice how the author frames the puzzle.
This objection assumes clarity is always better.
2
Read the answer carefully
The author provides the reason: the statement was made during a time of innovation. Read the Arabic and translation to see the full context.
3
Understand the historical context
The author points out that the early community still had righteous predecessors teaching everyone, even slaves and women. This created a baseline of sound knowledge.
This is key to understanding why 'old women's faith' was safe.
4
Reflect on the protective purpose
When innovations appeared, those with weak insight were told to stick to the simple faith of old women and children because it came directly from the Companions, untouched by innovation.
The phrase was a shield, not a sword.
5
Connect to the broader lesson
Consider how this passage defends the use of kalām and theological reasoning, showing that the phrase was not a blanket rejection but a contextual guidance.
This corrects a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : إذا كانَ مراد عمر بنِ عبدِ العَزِيزِ وَمَنْ ذُكِرَ معَهُ ما تَأَوَّلتَ فما بال اللفظِ عُدِلَ بهِ عن صريح المرادِ ؛ وذلكَ أنْ يُقال في جواب السائل مثلاً : ( عليك بما كان عليه الصحابة والسلف الصالح ) إلى أن قيل : عليكم بدين العجائز ، وعليك بدينِ الصبي... إلى آخره ؟ قلتُ : سبب ذلك والله أعلمُ : أنَّ تلك المقالة صدرَتْ منهم في زمان هيجان البدع ، ويدلُّ على ذلك سؤال الرجل عمر بن عبد العزيز الأهواء وكَانَ الزمانُ إِذْ ذاك لم يخلُ عن بقيَّةِ السلف الصالح المعتنين بالدين وبتعليمه للأهل والولد والأَمَةِ والعبدِ ، حتى كان الجميع يعرفون ما يخضُهم في دينهم أكمل معرفة ؛ امتثالاً لقولِهِ تعالى : ﴿ يَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا قُوا أَنفُسَكُمْ وَأَهْلِيكُمْ نَارًا) [التحريم : ٦] ، وليتَ أكابر علماء زماننا كانوا في معرفة السننِ مثل إماء علماء السلف الصالح أو نسائهم أو صبيانهم فلمَّا هاجَتِ البدعُ ، وخِيفَ على مَنْ هو ضعيفُ النظرِ أنْ يخرجَ إلى شيء منها .. قيل له : عليك بدين العجائز والصبيانِ ؛ لأنَّهم إنَّما اكتسبوهُ مِنْ تربية الصحابة والتابعين لهم بإحسانٍ ، والابتداعُ مِنْ قِبَلِهم
If you say: If the intention of ʿUmar ibn ʿAbd al-ʿAzīz and those mentioned with him is what you have interpreted, then why was the wording turned away from the clear intended meaning? For example, one should say in answer to the questioner: 'You must follow what the Companions and the righteous predecessors were upon,' up to the point where it was said: 'You must follow the religion of old women,' and 'You must follow the religion of a boy...' to the end? I say: The reason for that – and God knows best – is that that statement issued from them at a time when innovations were rampant. Evidence for that is the man's question to ʿUmar ibn ʿAbd al-ʿAzīz about whims (al-ahwāʾ). And the time then was not devoid of the remaining righteous predecessors who were concerned with religion and teaching it to their families, children, slave-girls, and slaves, such that all of them knew what concerned them in their religion with complete knowledge, in compliance with His statement, the Exalted: 'O you who have believed, protect yourselves and your families from a Fire' [At-Tahrīm: 6]. I wish that the major scholars of our time were in knowledge of the Sunnah like the slave-girls of the righteous predecessors or their women or their boys. Then when innovations appeared, and it was feared for one of weak insight that he might fall into something of them, it was said to him: 'You must follow the religion of old women and boys,' because they had only acquired it from the upbringing of the Companions and those who followed them in goodness, and innovation is from their [i.e., the innovators'] side.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection about the phrase 'religion of old women' (dīn al-ʿajāʾiz) attributed to ʿUmar ibn ʿAbd al-ʿAzīz and others. The objector asks: if the intended meaning was what the author claims (i.e., not a rejection of kalām), why did they use vague wording instead of saying 'follow the Companions' explicitly? The author answers that these statements were made at a time of rampant innovation (bidʿah). The context was that the early community still had righteous predecessors teaching religion thoroughly to all, even slaves and women, so everyone had sound basic knowledge. When innovations emerged, those with weak understanding were told to stick to the simple faith of old women and children—because that faith was acquired directly from the Companions and their successors, free from innovation. Thus, the phrase was a protective measure, not a denigration of theological reasoning.

دين العجائز
تقليد
اهواء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'religion of old women' means that simple, unquestioning faith is superior and that theological reasoning is forbidden.
Correction: The author explains that the phrase was a protective measure during times of innovation, directing those with weak insight to the safe, transmitted faith of the early community, not a rejection of all theological inquiry.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why did early scholars tell people to follow the 'religion of old women'?
A) Because old women are more pious
B) Because it was a time of innovation and they wanted to protect the weak from falling into it
C) Because scholarly knowledge is useless
D) Because the Quran commands it

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'religion of old women' was a protective measure during a time of innovation, directing the weak to the safe, transmitted faith of the early community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to follow the Sunnah, but do you rely more on your own reasoning or on what has been reliably transmitted from the Companions? When you are confused, do you seek out the simple, preserved faith of the early community, or do you engage in speculative debates? This lesson shows that even old women and children had sound knowledge—does your own faith have that same solid foundation, or is it built on shifting opinions? Will you commit to anchoring your beliefs in the transmitted teachings of the Salaf before diving into theological complexities?
?
Consider the time of innovation the Salaf faced: they directed the weak to the faith of old women. Are you willing to accept guidance from those you might consider less learned if their faith is purer and more authentic? What arrogance in your heart prevents you from learning from the simple, practicing Muslims who have preserved the deen through generations? This lesson exposes a danger: that you might be so caught up in your own intellect that you miss the safety of the straight path. Will you humble yourself and seek the religion of the 'old women'—the transmitted, practiced, and lived Islam?

Why the Salaf Said 'Follow the Religion of Old Women'
Sanusi answers why the Salaf advised weak believers to follow simple faith rather than scholarly debates.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the early Muslim scholars advised weak believers to follow the simple faith of old women and children, and how this advice protected them from heresies.

Core Idea
Simple faith was a fortress: the Salaf directed the weak to follow those untouched by heresy.

This passage addresses a common question: why did the Salaf use the phrase 'religion of old women' instead of simply saying 'follow the Companions'? Sanusi explains that this directive was a strategic measure during times of rampant heresies, when even claiming to follow the Companions had become ambiguous. By directing the weak to the pure, inherited faith of ordinary believers, the scholars provided a clear and safe path.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the opening question: why did the Salaf use indirect wording ('religion of old women') when they could have said 'follow the Companions' directly? Notice that this question sets up the need for an explanation.
The objector assumes the Salaf's words must have a deeper reason.
2
Follow the answer – historical context
Sanusi's answer begins by noting that these statements were made in a time of surging heresies. The Salaf had thoroughly taught the religion to everyone, including women, children, and slaves, so their faith was pure. When heresies appeared, the weak were directed to imitate those untouched by innovation.
The phrase 'weak in discernment' refers to those unable to navigate scholarly debates.
3
See the protective wisdom – the fortress analogy
Sanusi compares the simple faith of old women and children to a secure fortress. The weak believer enters this fortress for safety, while strong scholars stand guard outside, defending against heretics. This analogy clarifies why following the simple folk is a protective measure, not a downgrade.
The fortress represents a safe, unambiguous creed.
4
Recognize the danger of ambiguity
Sanusi explains that simply saying 'follow the Companions' would be ambiguous because every heretical group claims to follow the Companions. The specific directive to follow the old women and children avoids this confusion and gives clear guidance.
This shows the Salaf's concern for the weak in times of fitna.
5
Reflect on the role of strong scholars
The passage ends by noting that strong scholars defend the fortress and protect the weak. Al-Fakhr al-Razi himself, on his deathbed, is said to have sought refuge in the fortress of the weak. This underscores that the advice is not for everyone, but for those who cannot engage in theological debates.
The lesson is about context and humility, not anti-intellectualism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت: إذا كان مراد عمر بن عبد العزيز ومن ذكر معه ما تأولت فما بال اللفظ عدل به عن صريح المراد؟ وذلك أن يقال في جواب السائل مثلا: (عليك بما كان عليه الصحابة والسلف الصالح) إلى أن قيل: عليكم بدين العجائز، وعليك بدين الصبيان؟ قلت: سبب ذلك والله أعلم: أن تلك المقالة صدرت منهم في زمان هيجان البدع، ويدل على ذلك سؤال الرجل عمر بن عبد العزيز الأهواء وكان الزمان إذ ذاك لم يخل عن بقية السلف الصالح المعتنين بالدين وبتعليمه للأهل والولد والأمة والعبد، حتى كان الجميع يعرفون ما يخصهم في دينهم أكمل معرفة؛ امتثالا لقول تعالى: {يأيها الذين آمنوا قوا أنفسكم وأهليكم نارا} [التحريم:6]، وليت أكابر علماء زماننا كانوا في معرفة السنن مثل إماء علماء السلف الصالح أو نسائهم أو صبيانهم. فلما هاجت البدع، وخيف على من هو ضعيف النظر أن يخرج إلى شيء منها .. قيل له: عليك بدين العجائز والصبيان؛ لأنهم إنما اكتسبوه من تربية الصحابة والتابعين لهم بإحسان، والابتداع من قبلهم مأمون، وأهل البدع لا يقصدونهم بالمخالطة، فأمنوا من التلوث بأقذار البدع على عقائدهم التي أتقنوها؛ بما يحتاج إليه من البراهين، على حسب ما أخذوه من السلف الصالح، وفهموه من الكتاب والسنة؛ لسهولة ذلك عليهم؛ إذ هم عرب لم تستول على ألسنتهم العجمة، ولا صعد على قلوبهم ران الجمود ولا ظلمة الغباوة، فعقائدهم أسلم شيء وأحسنه، فلهذا أمر ضعيف النظر أن ينتمي إلى حرز دينهم المأمون؛ لعدم المخالطة لأهل البدع، ولوقوف أئمة زمانهم المتسعين في الأنظار، ولهم القوة العظمى في الذهن واللسان رضي الله عنهم .. أمام حرز دينهم، يدفعون عنهم كل مبتدع وضال، وتحملوا في ذلك رضي الله عنهم من مشاق النظر والإذاية في الأنفس والمال ما يعظم الله به أجورهم. ولو قيل لضعيف النظر الذي حيرته الأهواء: عليك بما عليه الصحابة.. لكان إحالة على جهالة؛ إذ كل من أهل البدع يدعي أن ما ينتحله هو مذهب الصحابة، فكان من الحزم والصواب ما أمر به علماء السلف من الانتماء إلى الحرز المأمون الذي وقفت أبطال العلماء لمناضلة أعداء الدين أمامه، والضعيف إذا لم يدخل الحرز ووقف موقف الأبطال .. خيف عليه أن يهلكه العدو لضعفه. ولهذا أيضاً مال الفخر في موطن الموت لحرز الضعفاء ودعا به؛
If you say: If the intention of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz and those mentioned with him was what you interpreted, then why was the wording diverted from the explicit intended meaning? That is, why is it said in answer to the questioner, for example: ('Upon you is what the Companions and the righteous predecessors were upon') until it was said: 'Upon you is the religion of old women,' and 'Upon you is the religion of children'? I say: The reason for that, and God knows best, is that that statement issued from them in a time of the surge of heresies. Evidence for that is the question of the man to Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz about the sects, and the time then was not devoid of the remaining righteous predecessors who were concerned with religion and teaching it to family, children, slave-girls, and slaves, until all of them knew what concerned them in their religion with complete knowledge, in compliance with His statement, the Exalted: 'O you who have believed, protect yourselves and your families from a Fire' [At-Tahrim:6]. Would that the senior scholars of our time were in knowledge of the Sunna like the female servants of the scholars of the righteous predecessors, or their women, or their children. Then when heresies surged, and it was feared for one weak in discernment that he might go out to something of them, it was said to him: 'Upon you is the religion of old women and children,' because they acquired it only from the upbringing of the Companions and the Followers who followed them in excellence, and innovation from their side is secure, and the people of heresy do not intend to mix with them, so they are safe from being polluted by the filth of heresies upon their creeds which they had perfected with what is needed of proofs, according to what they took from the righteous predecessors and understood from the Book and the Sunna, due to the ease of that for them, since they were Arabs whose tongues were not dominated by non-Arabic, nor did the rust of stagnation or the darkness of dullness ascend upon their hearts, so their creeds are the safest thing and the best. For this reason, the weak in discernment was commanded to adhere to the secure fortress of their religion, due to the absence of mixing with the people of heresy, and because of the standing of the leading scholars of their time, who were expansive in insights, and they have the greatest power in intellect and tongue, may God be pleased with them, before the fortress of their religion, who repel from them every innovator and deviant, and they undertook in that, may God be pleased with them, from the hardships of investigation and harm in persons and wealth, what God magnifies their rewards with. And if it were said to the weak in discernment whom the sects have confused: 'Upon you is what the Companions were upon,' it would be a referral to ignorance, since every one of the people of heresy claims that what he adopts is the doctrine of the Companions. So it was from resoluteness and correctness what the scholars of the predecessors commanded: adherence to the secure fortress before which the champions of the scholars stood for combating the enemies of religion. And the weak one, if he does not enter the fortress and stands in the position of champions, it is feared that the enemy will destroy him due to his weakness. And for this reason also, al-Fakhr inclined in the time of death to the fortress of the weak and called for it.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector asks: if the Salaf intended to guide people to the way of the Companions, why did they use the specific phrase 'religion of old women and children' instead of just saying 'follow the Companions'? The answer begins by stating that these statements were made in an era when heresies were rampant. At that time, ordinary believers—women, children, slaves—had learned the religion directly from the Salaf and were untouched by heretical sects. Their faith was pure and safe. So directing the weak to follow them was like directing them to a secure fortress. Moreover, simply saying 'follow the Companions' would be ambiguous because every heretical group claims to follow the Companions. The specific directive to follow the simple faith of the innocents avoided confusion. The author also likens the weak person to someone who cannot fight; he should take refuge in the fortress while the strong scholars defend the faith. The mention of al-Fakhr (likely Fakhr al-Din al-Razi) at the end reinforces this point.

عمر بن عبد العزيز
بدع
ضعيف النظر
حرز
العجائز
الصبيان
البراهين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Salaf's advice to follow the religion of old women encourages intellectual laziness and blind following.
Correction: The passage shows that this advice was a protective measure for the weak in a time of heresies, not a general anti-intellectual stance. Strong scholars were still engaged in defense of the faith.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why did Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz and other Salaf advise the weak to follow the religion of old women and children rather than simply saying 'follow the Companions'?
A) Because old women and children have purer faith than the Companions.
B) Because every heretical group claims to follow the Companions, so that advice would be ambiguous.
C) Because the weak are incapable of understanding the Companions' way.
D) Because the Salaf did not respect the Companions.

Key Takeaway
The Salaf's directive to follow the religion of old women and children was a strategic, context-specific measure to protect the weak from heresies, not a general dismissal of theological knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter confusing theological debates online or in lectures, do you humbly retreat to the clear faith you learned from your parents or teachers, or do you venture into arguments without sufficient knowledge? What will you do next time?
?
The Salaf taught their families even the finest details of the Sunna. Have you ensured that those under your care — your children, spouse, or close friends — have a fortified, simple faith that can withstand the heresies of our time? If not, what step will you take this week?
?
Al-Fakhr al-Razi, a master of theology, turned to the fortress of the weak on his deathbed. What does that say about the ultimate safety of the heart? Are you building your faith on pride in knowledge or on humble submission? Be honest and commit to one change.

Warning Against al-Razi's Theological Works
Two classical critiques of al-Razi's theological writings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why classical scholars warned against the theological writings of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, focusing on al-Maqqari's and Ibn Taymiyya's criticisms.

Core Idea
Al-Razi excels at formulating doubts but fails to resolve them properly.

This passage presents two classical critiques of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's theological method. Al-Maqqari observes that al-Razi is better at formulating doubts than refuting them, while Ibn Taymiyya's poetry condemns his work as 'inspiration of devils.' These warnings remind us that theological inquiry must always be anchored in religious commitment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English versions to get an overall sense of the criticisms.
Notice the chain of transmission in Ibn Taymiyya's poem.
2
Analyze al-Maqqari's criticism
Focus on the phrase 'أشد منه في تقرير الشبه' and understand the imbalance between presenting and refuting doubts.
This is a serious charge for a theologian.
3
Examine Ibn Taymiyya's poetry
Study the wordplay on 'Muhassal/Tahsil' and the charge of 'وحي الشياطين'.
Consider why such strong language is used.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شنيع أهوائهم ، ولهذا يُحذِّرُ الشيوخ مِنَ النظر في كثيرٍ مِنْ تواليفه . قال الشيخ أبو عبدِ اللهِ محمَّدُ بنُ محمدِ بنِ أَحمدَ المَقَرِيُّ التِّلِمْسانِيُّ رحمَهُ الله تعالى ورضي عنه : ( مَنْ تَحقَّقَ كلام ابن الخطيب وجدَه في تقريرِ الشُّبَهِ أَشدَّ منه في الانفصال عنها ، وفي هذا ما لا يخفى )(۱) ( أنشدني شيخي أبو عبدِ اللهِ الآبُليُّ ، قالَ : أَنشدني عبد اللهِ بنُ إبراهيمَ الزَّمُّوري، قال: أنشدني تقي الدين بن تيمية لنفسه (۲) : [من البسيط] مُحَصَّلُ فِي أُصُولِ الدِّينِ حَاصِلُهُ مِنْ بَعْدِ « تَحْصِيلِهِ » عِلْمٌ بِلَا دِينِ أَصْلُ الضَّلَالَةِ فِي الْإِفْكِ الْمُبِينِ فَمَا فِيهِ فَأَكْثَرُهُ وَحْيُ الشَّيَاطِينِ
Foul are their desires, and for this reason the shaykhs warn against looking into many of his writings. Al-Shaykh Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Maqqari al-Tilimsani, may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him, said: 'Whoever examines the words of Ibn al-Khatib finds him more severe in presenting the doubts than in separating from them, and in this is what is not hidden.' (1) (My shaykh Abu Abdullah al-Abuli recited to me, he said: Abdullah ibn Ibrahim al-Zammuri recited to me, he said: Taqi al-Din ibn Taymiyya recited to me for himself (2): [al-basit] The Muhassal in the principles of religion, its result after its 'tahsil' is knowledge without religion. The origin of misguidance in clear falsehood, so what is in it, most of it is the inspiration of devils.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage presents two criticisms of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi (Ibn al-Khatib). First, al-Maqqari states that whoever examines al-Razi's writings finds him more skilled at presenting doubts (shubuhāt) than at resolving them (infisāl). This is a serious charge because the purpose of kalam is to refute doubts. Second, Ibn Taymiyya's poetry attacks al-Razi's book 'Muhassal fī Uṣūl al-Dīn' by saying its result is 'knowledge without religion' and that most of its content is 'inspiration of devils.' The poetry is transmitted through a chain of reciters, showing its authenticity. The passage is a warning against excessive immersion in philosophical kalam.

Key Terms
تقرير الشبه
الانفصال
محصل
تحصيل
وحي الشياطين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the criticism of al-Razi implies he was not a sincere Muslim scholar.
Correction: The passage shows the criticism is about method (presenting doubts vs. resolving them), not about his faith.

Checkpoint
According to al-Maqqari, what is the problem with Ibn al-Khatib's (al-Razi's) theological writings?
A) He is weak in presenting doubts.
B) He is stronger in presenting doubts than in resolving them.
C) He writes for political reasons.
D) His works are too long.

Key Takeaway
Classical scholars warned against al-Razi's method because he could state doubts more powerfully than he could refute them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a doubt about your faith, are you more skilled at articulating or refuting it? Which tendency do you cultivate, and what does that reveal about your heart's orientation toward truth?
?
Al-Razi's book is described as 'knowledge without religion.' Is there any area of your religious knowledge that has become merely academic—studied for its own sake rather than to draw you closer to Allah? What would it take for your learning to become 'knowledge with religion'?
?
Ibn Taymiyya attributes the content of al-Razi's book to 'the inspiration of devils.' Are there any sources of knowledge you regularly turn to—books, speakers, websites—that might be subtly undermining your trust in revelation? Ask Allah to protect you from intellectual deception.

Defending al-Razi: His State at Death
Author relates anecdote of a critic and explains al-Razi's deathbed poetry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's defense of al-Razi's deathbed state and the significance of his poetry in kalam thought.

Core Idea
Al-Razi's deathbed poetry reveals a retreat to taqlid from fear of doubt, not disbelief.

This passage presents a controversial anecdote about Fakhr al-Din al-Razi and a critic who would have struck him. The author, a later Ash'ari scholar, defends al-Razi by interpreting his deathbed poetry as a sincere expression of fear and regret, not heresy. By studying this, we see how kalam scholars handled doubts and the role of taqlid.

Guided Path
1
Encounter the anecdote
Read the anecdote about the critic who wanted to strike al-Razi with a staff. Notice the accusation implied.
This sets up the problem: al-Razi's orthodoxy is questioned.
2
Read the author's hypothesis
The author suggests al-Razi faced unresolved doubts at death and feared them, leading him to wish for the safety of taqlid.
This is the author's defense strategy.
3
Examine the deathbed poetry
Read the poem al-Razi recited at death. Note its themes: limitation of intellect, harm of world, useless research.
The poem supports the author's interpretation.
4
Analyze the two interpretations
The author presents two probabilities: either al-Razi truly sought refuge in taqlid out of fear, or he expressed regret. Also note the mention of 'elderly women' as those with minimal belief.
This shows the author's careful theological reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : وكانَ بيدِهِ قضيب ، فقال : لو أدركتُ فخر الدينِ لَضربتُهُ بقضيبي هذا على رأسه ) انتهى (۱) قلتُ : فلعل الفخرَ  َرحمَهُ اللهُ تعالى حضرَ لهُ عندَ المَوتِ مِنَ الشُّبَهِ التي عَسُرَ عليه الانفصال عنها .. ما حمله الخوفُ منهُ أنْ تَمَنَّى أن يكونَ [ من الطويل] في درجة الاعتقادِ التقليدي ، لأنَّ رأيه فيهِ أنَّهُ كافٍ ، وقد رُوِيَ عنهُ أَنَّهُ أنشد عند الموتِ (۲) : نِهَايَةُ أَقْدَامِ (۳) الْعُقُولِ عِقَالُ وَأَكْثَرُ سَعْيِ الْعَالِمِينَ ضَلَالُ وَأَرْوَاحُنَا فِي وَحْشَةٍ مِنْ جُسُومِنَا وَحَاصِلُ دُنْيَانَا أَذِيَّ وَوَبَالُ وَلَمْ نَسْتَفِدْ مِنْ بَحْيِنَا طُولَ عُمْرِنَا سِوَى أَنْ جَمَعْنَا فِيهِ قِيلَ وَقَالُوا وَكَمْ مِنْ رِجَالٍ قَدْ رَأَيْنَا وَدَوْلَةٍ فَبَادُوا جَمِيعاً مُسْرِعِينَ وَزَالُوا وَكَمْ مِنْ جِبَالٍ قَدْ عَلَتْ شُرُفَاتِهَا رِجَالٌ فَمَاتُوا وَالْجِبَالُ جِبَالُ فعلى هذا الاحتمال يكونُ الفخرُ تمنَّى لِعِظَمِ الخوفِ الدخول في حرْزِ المقلدين حقيقةً ، أو على معنى التلهف والندم على ما فاتَ ويحتملُ أنْ يكونَ معَ هاذا أرادَ بالعجائز العجائز المقتصراتِ على القَدْرِ الضروري في تصحيح العقائدِ ؛ إِذْ هو حال عجائز ذلكَ الزمانِ وما قبلَهُ مِنَ الأزمنة الفاضلة كما قدَّمنا (٤) ، وبهذا تعرفُ أنَّ هذا
He said: And in his hand was a staff, so he said: 'If I had found Fakhr al-Din, I would have struck him on his head with this staff of mine.' End. (1) I say: Perhaps Fakhr, may Allah have mercy on him, had at death the presence of doubts from which it was difficult for him to separate, and the fear from them drove him to wish to be, [in the meter al-tawil], in the degree of imitative belief (taqlid), because his view regarding it was that it is sufficient. And it has been narrated from him that he recited at death (2): The ultimate limit of the feet of intellects is a shackle, and most of the striving of scholars is misguidance. And our souls are in loneliness from our bodies, and the result of our world is harm and calamity. And we have not benefited from our research throughout our lives except that we have gathered in it 'qila wa qalu' (idle talk). And how many men and dynasties have we seen, and they all perished quickly and passed away. And how many mountains whose peaks men have ascended, then they died and the mountains remained mountains. So upon this probability, Fakhr wished, due to the greatness of fear, to enter the fortress of the muqallids (imitators) truly, or in the sense of longing and regret for what had passed. And it is possible that he meant by 'old women' (al-'ajā'iz) the old women who limit themselves to the necessary amount in correcting beliefs, for that was the condition of the old women of that time and before it of the virtuous ages, as we have presented (4). And by this you know that this...
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage begins with an anecdote: a critic says that if he had met Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, he would have struck him with a stick. The author (presumably Sanusi or the commentator) then speculates on al-Razi's state at death. He suggests that perhaps al-Razi faced so many unresolved doubts at death that he feared them and wished to be in the position of a muqallid (one who follows authority without reasoning), because al-Razi believed taqlid was sufficient. Then the author quotes al-Razi's deathbed poetry expressing that the ultimate limit of intellects is stagnation, most effort is misguidance, and that life's conclusion is nothing but 'qīla wa qālū' (idle talk). The author interprets this as either a genuine desire to be in the safety of taqlid due to great fear, or as an expression of regret. He also notes that al-Razi might have been referring to the elderly women ('ajā'iz) of his time who limited themselves to the minimum necessary for correct belief, which was the practice of virtuous ages. The passage thus defends al-Razi against claims of heresy by explaining his state as one of fear and regret rather than disbelief.

Key Terms
مقلد
اعتقاد تقليدي
عجائز
شبه
قيل وقالوا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Razi died as a skeptic or heretic.
Correction: The author explains that al-Razi's state was due to fear of unresolved doubts, leading him to wish for taqlid, and his poetry is not evidence of disbelief but of regret and the limitations of reason.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why did al-Razi wish to be in the degree of taqlid (imitative belief) at death?
A) He became a skeptic.
B) He feared the unresolved doubts.
C) He regretted his intellectual efforts.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's deathbed state is interpreted as a retreat to taqlid due to overwhelming doubt, not evidence of disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a doubt about your faith that you cannot resolve, do you trust that Allah will accept your reliance on the simple beliefs of a ‘common believer’? Or do you let that doubt grow into despair? What would it take for you to say, like al-Razi, ‘I wish I were like an old woman’?
?
Al-Razi spent his life in deep research, yet at death he called most of it ‘idle talk.’ If you knew you would die tonight, which parts of your current pursuit of Islamic knowledge would you regret, and which would you be confident are truly beneficial? What change can you make starting today?
?
A critic wanted to strike al-Razi for his supposed deviation. But the author defended him by giving a charitable interpretation. When you hear about a Muslim scholar or fellow believer struggling with doubts, are you quick to condemn or do you seek excuses? What would it cost you to extend the same benefit of the doubt that the author gave to al-Razi?

Refuting the Ignorance of the Sahaba Argument
Sanusi refutes the argument that the Sahaba did not know kalam terms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Sahaba's unfamiliarity with later kalam terms does not indicate ignorance of the proofs of faith.

Core Idea
Technical terms are not the proofs themselves; they are just labels.

Sanusi begins by addressing a common argument used by proponents of blind following: that the Sahaba died without knowing terms like jawhar and 'arad. He refutes this with logical reasoning and a striking analogy, showing that ignorance of terminology does not imply ignorance of the actual evidences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the author's tone of astonishment and the analogy he uses.
The analogy compares kalam terminology to grammar terms that were coined later.
2
Identify the structure of the refutation
The author presents the opponent's claim, expresses amazement, gives an analogy, and then states the real condition for valid argument.
3
Reflect on the condition
The author says the argument would only hold if the Sahaba abandoned reflection (nazar) and did not understand Quranic proofs. Why is that condition impossible?
This connects to the learning objective.

وأَمَّا الأَوَّلُ ـ وهو قوله : مات أبو بكر وعمر رضي الله عنهما ولم يعرفا الجوهر والعَرَضَ ، وكذلك سائر الصحابة رضوان الله عليهم - : فأنا أعجبُ أنْ يَذكُرَ مثلَ هذا دليلاً على التقليدِ مَنْ لَهُ أدنى تمييز ، فأَيُّ للألفاظ المصطلح عليها في شيءٍ مِنْ أَدلَّةِ العقائدِ حتى يلزمَ مِنَ الجهل بشيء منها الجهلُ بشيءٍ مِنَ الأدلَّةِ ؟! مدخل وما أشبه هذا بقولِ مَنْ يقولُ : إِنَّ الصحابة رضوانُ اللهِ عليهم كانَتْ تجهل المقصودَ مِنْ علم العربيةِ ؛ لأنَّهم ماتوا ولم يعرفوا حقيقةً الفاعل ولا المفعول ولا الحالِ والتمييز المصطلح عليها عند علماء العربية ، أو كانوا يجهلونَ المقصودَ مِنَ البلاغة ؛ لأنَّهم كانوا يجهلونَ ألفاظاً فيها أحدثها مَنْ بعدهم اصطلاحاً ! وهل هذه الأقوال تصدرُ مِنْ عاقل أُلهِم رشدَهُ ؟! وإِنَّما يصح لهُ الاستدلال لو ثبتَ لهُ أنَّ الصحابة رضوان الله عليهم ماتوا ولم يعرفوا اللهَ إلا بمُجرَّدِ التقليدِ ، وأعرضوا عن النظرِ الذي حصّ تعالى عليه في آي مِنْ كتابِهِ ، وأنَّ أدلَّةَ العقائدِ التي لا تُحصى كثرةً في القرآنِ كانَتْ تمرُّ عليهم ولم يفهموا وجه دلالتِها ، وصحة هذا عنهم مما يأباه كلُّ مؤمن . [ حدَّةُ ذكاء الصحابة الكرامِ رضيَ الله عنهم ووفور علمهم ] وما أحوج مَنْ يُعرِّضُ بمثل هذهِ النقيصة في علي مناصبهم التي لا تُلحَقُ .. لعظيم الأدب ! ولقد نقطعُ أنَّ أكابر علماء زماننا لم يحصل لهم مِنَ العلم بالدين وسننه ما حصل لأدنى أَمَةٍ مِنْ إماء الصحابة رضي الله عنهم أو صبي مُميَّز مِنْ صبيانهم ، وكذا التابعون وتابعوهم بإحسان . ولقد أدرك علي رضي الله عنه زمنَ المبتدعة ، وأفحمهم بما لم يقدروا أن يجدوا معه جواباً ، وحُكِيَ عنه رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ أَنَّهُ قالَ : ( لو أذنَ لي رسولُ اللهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أنْ أضعَ على « الفاتحةِ » وِقْرَ سبعين بعيراً.. لفعلتُ ) (۱) ، وقالَ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : ( أَنَا مَدِينَةٌ الْعِلْم وَعَلِيٌّ بَابُهَا ) (۲) ، وقد نُقِلَ عنه رضي الله عنه في كل علم العجب العُجاب ، حتى افتتنت بهِ طوائفُ مِنَ المبتدعة وادَّعى بعضُهم فيهِ ما ادَّعَتْهُ النصارى في عيسى عليه السلام . ( ومن عجيبِ أمرِه رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ : أَنَّ مُعضلاتِ المسائل التي لا يُتوصل إلى جوابها إلا بالأنظارِ الدقيقة في السنين المتطاولة .. إذا سُئِلَ هو عنها أجابَ عنها بديهةً مِنْ غيرِ تأمل ولا تعظيم لشأنها ، كأنَّها عنده سؤال الأمور الضرورية ؛ ككون الاثنين مثلاً أكثرَ مِنَ عن الواحد ، وقضاياه في ذلك مشهورةٌ مسطورةٌ في الكُتُب ، وتأمل جوابه رضي الله عنه على المنبر في الفريضة المنبرية ؛ وهي : زوجة وابنتان وأبوان ، وقوله على البديهة بلا تأمل ولا تأخُرٍ في ذلك الموقفِ الصعب : ( صارَ ثُمنُها تُشعاً ) (۳) ، ثم اعرض على عقول أكثر الناسِ ذلك وانظر أين هم ممَّا هنالك
As for the first argument—namely his statement: 'Abu Bakr and 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) died not knowing jawhar (substance) and 'arad (accident), and likewise the rest of the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them)'—I am amazed that someone with the least discernment would mention such a thing as evidence for taqlid (blind following). For what connection do the conventionally coined terms have with the proofs of beliefs, so that ignorance of some of them would entail ignorance of some of the proofs?! This resembles the statement of one who says: 'The Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) were ignorant of the purpose of the science of Arabic, because they died without knowing the true nature of the subject (al-fa'il), the object (al-maf'ul), the state (al-hal), and the distinction (al-tamyiz) as conventionally defined by grammarians,' or 'they were ignorant of the purpose of balagha (rhetoric) because they were ignorant of terms coined by later generations as conventions.' Could such statements come from an intelligent person inspired with guidance?! His argument would only be valid if it were established that the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) died knowing Allah only through mere taqlid, and turned away from the reflection (al-nazar) that the Exalted urged in verses of His Book, and that the countless proofs of beliefs in the Qur'an passed them by without their understanding their evidential import. The truth of this about them is something every believer rejects. [The sharpness of intelligence of the noble Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, and the abundance of their knowledge] How much more necessary is great politeness for one who exposes himself to such a deficiency in the lofty stations of those whose stations cannot be attained! We are certain that the leading scholars of our time have not attained from knowledge of the religion and its ways what the lowest female servant of the female servants of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, or a discerning child among their children attained, likewise the Followers and those who followed them in goodness. And indeed 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) encountered the era of the innovators (al-mubtadi'a) and silenced them such that they found no answer. It is narrated from him (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: 'If the Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) had permitted me to place on the Fatiha the load of seventy camels, I would have done so.' And he (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) said: 'I am the city of knowledge and 'Ali is its gate.' It has been reported from him (may Allah be pleased with him) regarding every science that which is wondrously amazing, to the extent that groups of innovators were seduced by him and some claimed about him what the Christians claimed about Jesus (peace be upon him). And among the amazing aspects of his matter (may Allah be pleased with him) is that difficult problems that cannot be solved except by precise reflection over many years—when asked about them, he would answer instinctively without reflection or magnifying their importance, as if they were for him like questions about necessary matters, such as that two is greater than one, for example. His judgments in that regard are famous and recorded in books. Consider his answer (may Allah be pleased with him) on the pulpit regarding the minbar inheritance case: a wife, two daughters, and two parents. He said instinctively without reflection or delay in that difficult situation: 'Her eighth has become a ninth.' Then present that to the minds of most people and see where they are relative to that.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an argument used by proponents of taqlid (blind following) who claimed that the Sahaba (Companions) did not use kalam terminology like jawhar (substance) and 'arad (accident), and therefore such terminology is unnecessary for faith. The author first expresses astonishment that anyone with discernment would cite this as evidence for taqlid. He argues that the technical terms of kalam have no necessary connection to the actual proofs of beliefs in the Qur'an; ignorance of terms does not imply ignorance of proofs. To illustrate, he provides an analogy: if someone argued that the Sahaba were ignorant of the purpose of Arabic grammar because they did not use the technical terms of grammarians like fa'il, maf'ul, hal, or tamyiz, that would be absurd. Similarly, claiming they were ignorant of rhetoric because they lacked later terminology is equally absurd. The author then questions the rationality of such statements. He states that the opponent's argument would only be valid if it could be proven that the Sahaba died knowing Allah only through taqlid and turned away from the reflection (nazar) that Allah commanded in the Qur'an, and that they did not understand the evidences in the Qur'an—something no believer can accept. The author then praises the intelligence and knowledge of the Sahaba, asserting that even the greatest scholars of later times have not attained the level of religious knowledge that the least of the Sahaba or even their servants and discerning children possessed. This extends also to the Followers and the next generation. Next, the author focuses on 'Ali ibn Abi Talib as a prime example. He relates that 'Ali encountered the innovators and silenced them. He quotes 'Ali saying that if the Prophet had allowed him, he could have placed the entire knowledge of the Qur'an (symbolized by the Fatiha) on seventy camels. He also cites the famous hadith 'I am the city of knowledge and 'Ali is its gate.' The author notes that 'Ali's knowledge was so vast that some innovators were seduced by him and made exaggerated claims about him, similar to what Christians claim about Jesus. Finally, the author gives a specific example of 'Ali's instinctive knowledge: the 'minbar inheritance case' (al-farida al-minbariyya) where a wife, two daughters, and two parents were heirs. Normally, the wife receives 1/8, but the shares add up to more than one. 'Ali solved it on the spot by turning the wife's share from 1/8 to 1/9 (making total 1/9 + 2/3 + 1/3 + 1/3 = ? actually 1/9 + 2/3 + 1/3 + 1/3 = 1/9 + 2/3 + 2/3 = 1/9 + 4/3 = 1/9 + 12/9 = 13/9 >1, but the traditional solution is to reduce the shares proportionally, and the famous answer 'صار ثمنها تسعا' means her eighth became a ninth. The author presents this as evidence of 'Ali's extraordinary intellect. He concludes by challenging the reader to compare the minds of most people to 'Ali's.

Key Terms
الجوهر والعرض
التقليد
النظر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Sahaba were ignorant of kalam terminology, so using such terms is unnecessary or even blameworthy.
Correction: Sanusi explains that ignorance of coined terms does not imply ignorance of the actual proofs of faith. The Sahaba understood the Quranic evidences deeply, even without later theological vocabulary.

Checkpoint
What analogy does Sanusi use to refute the argument about the Sahaba not knowing kalam terms?
A) The Sahaba were like grammarians who knew all technical terms.
B) Claiming the Sahaba were ignorant of Arabic because they didn't know grammar terms.
C) The Sahaba were like philosophers who used different terms.
D) The Sahaba were all illiterate, so terms don't matter.

Key Takeaway
The Sahaba's lack of familiarity with later kalam terminology does not prove they relied on taqlid; they knew the actual proofs from the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you explain your faith to others, do you rely more on theological jargon or on direct engagement with Quranic verses? Which approach would the Sahaba have taken?
?
Are there areas of your belief that you have accepted from family or culture without personally reflecting (nazar) on the evidence from Allah's Book? What is one verse you can commit to pondering this week as a proof for something you believe?
?
If an opponent used the same flawed reasoning as in this passage—judging you based on your lack of familiarity with certain terms—how would you respond? Are you quick to dismiss others' lack of terminology as ignorance, or do you look for their actual understanding of the proofs?

The Profound Knowledge of the Sahaba
Sanusi affirms the superior knowledge of the Sahaba over later scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will appreciate the immense religious knowledge that the Sahaba and the early generations possessed, surpassing later scholars.

Core Idea
The least of the Sahaba exceeded later scholars in knowledge.

After refuting the negative argument, Sanusi positively affirms the high level of knowledge among the Sahaba. He makes a bold claim: even the greatest scholars of later times have not attained what the lowest servant of the Sahaba possessed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the strong language of certainty ('we are certain').
2
Identify the comparison
The author compares leading scholars of his time to the lowest female servant of the Sahaba and a discerning child. What is he emphasizing?
3
Reflect on the implication
If even the servants and children of the Sahaba were so knowledgeable, what does that say about the Sahaba themselves?

( ومن عجيبِ أمرِه رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ : أَنَّ مُعضلاتِ المسائل التي لا يُتوصل إلى جوابها إلا بالأنظارِ الدقيقة في السنين المتطاولة .. إذا سُئِلَ هو عنها أجابَ عنها بديهةً مِنْ غيرِ تأمل ولا تعظيم لشأنها ، كأنَّها عنده سؤال الأمور الضرورية ؛ ككون الاثنين مثلاً أكثرَ مِنَ عن الواحد ، وقضاياه في ذلك مشهورةٌ مسطورةٌ في الكُتُب ، وتأمل جوابه رضي الله عنه على المنبر في الفريضة المنبرية ؛ وهي : زوجة وابنتان وأبوان ، وقوله على البديهة بلا تأمل ولا تأخُرٍ في ذلك الموقفِ الصعب : ( صارَ ثُمنُها تُشعاً ) (۳) ، ثم اعرض على عقول أكثر الناسِ ذلك وانظر أين هم ممَّا هنالك
As for the first argument—namely his statement: 'Abu Bakr and 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) died not knowing jawhar (substance) and 'arad (accident), and likewise the rest of the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them)'—I am amazed that someone with the least discernment would mention such a thing as evidence for taqlid (blind following). Commentary
